Obligations When Aman Is Unknowingly Violated
Ruling on unknowing violation of aman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligations imposed on Muslims who unknowingly violate an aman and explain why children are free Muslims.

Core Idea
Violation of aman unknowingly requires diya, return of captives and property, and mahr; children follow father's free status.

This passage from al-Tatarkhaniyyah addresses a scenario where Muslim soldiers mistakenly attack a group that had been granted aman (safe conduct). When the aman becomes known, the law imposes specific compensatory obligations. Understanding this ruling clarifies how Islamic law protects the inviolability of aman and rectifies honest errors in warfare.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act: Muslims unknowingly killed and captured people who had aman. The ruling: they must pay diya for each killed, return captives and property, and pay mahr for consummation.
This is a positive obligation (wajib) arising from unintentional violation.
2
List the specific obligations
1. Diya for killed persons. 2. Return captured women and property to owners. 3. Pay full mahr for each woman with whom intercourse occurred. 4. Children born are free Muslims – no compensation.
Each obligation has a distinct legal rationale: diya compensates for life, mahr for sexual access, return for property.
3
Note the procedure for returning women
Women are returned after completing their ʿiddah (three menstrual periods). During ʿiddah, they are placed in custody of a trustworthy old woman, not a man.
This ensures the women are not in a prohibited situation and their waiting period is observed.
4
Analyze the status of children
Children are free Muslims following their father's status. No compensation (qima) is required.
This is based on the principle that the child's status follows the superior status of the parents – the father is free and Muslim.
5
Identify the source authority
The ruling is cited from al-Tatarkhaniyyah, a later Hanafi fatwa collection (fatawa mutakhkhirin).
This indicates the ruling is part of the operative fatwa tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أولاد آخرون من المسلمين قتلوا الرجل وسبوا النساء والأموال واقتسموا ذلك وولد لهم منهن ثم علموا بالأمان فعلى الذين قتلوا دية من قتلوا وترد النساء والأموال إلى أهلها وتغرم للنساء أصدقتهن لما أصابوا من فروجهن والأولاد أحرار مسلمون تبعاً لأبيهم لكن إنما ترد النساء بعد ثلاث حيض، وفي زمان الاعتداد يوضعن على يدي عدل والعدل امرأة عجوز ثقة لا الرجل، ويكون الأولاد أحراراً بغير قيمة؛ كذا في التتارخانية .اهـ.
Some other Muslims killed the man, captured the women and property, divided that, and children were born to them from those women, then they learned of the aman. So upon those who killed is the blood-money for whom they killed, and the women and property are returned to their owners, and they pay the women their bridal gifts (mahr) for what they had intercourse with them, and the children are free Muslims following their father. However, the women are only returned after three menstrual periods, and during the period of waiting they are placed in the custody of a just person, and the just person is a trustworthy old woman, not a man. And the children are free without any compensation. Thus in al-Tatarkhaniyyah.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi school concerning a scenario where a group of Muslims unwittingly kill and capture people from a party that had been granted aman (safe conduct) by the Muslim authorities. When the aman later becomes known, the Muslims who killed must pay full diya (blood-money) for each person killed. The captured women and property must be returned to their original owners. For the women, the Muslims must also pay their full mahr (bridal gift) as compensation for intercourse. The children born from such unions are free Muslims, following the status of their father, and no compensation (qima) is required. This reflects the principle that the father's status determines the child's, and since the father is Muslim and free, the child is also Muslim and free. The women are returned after completing their 'iddah (waiting period of three menstrual cycles), and during that period they are placed in the custody of a trustworthy old woman, not a man, to ensure propriety. The ruling is cited from al-Tatarkhaniyyah, a later Hanafi work, indicating it is part of the fatwa literature (fatawa mutakhkhirin).

Key Terms
أمان (amān): Safe conduct granted to enemies guaranteeing security for their lives and property.
دية (diya): Blood-money or financial compensation paid for wrongful killing.
عدة (ʿiddah): Waiting period for a woman after separation from her husband, during which she cannot remarry.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They are slaves who must be compensated with qima
B) They are free Muslims following their father's status
C) They are slaves and belong to the original owners
D) They are free but must be ransomed

Key Takeaway
When aman is unknowingly violated, Muslims must fully compensate the victims, and children born from such unions are free Muslims following their father's status.

Nature and Types of Aman
Defines aman as non-binding, two types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of aman (safe conduct), explain why it is a non-binding contract, and distinguish between its two types: absolute and time-bound.

Core Idea
Aman is a non-binding contract revocable by the imam for maslaha, either absolute (revocable) or time-bound (expires automatically).

In the previous lesson, we learned about the general concept of aman. Now we delve into its legal nature. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes that aman is not a binding contract but a revocable one, grounded in maslaha. It also introduces the two categories: absolute and time-bound aman, each with distinct rules for termination. Let's work through the key points.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal classification
What is aman? It is a contract of safe conduct granted to enemies. Determine its hukm (legal ruling) according to the Hanafi school.
2
Determine the binding nature
Is aman binding or non-binding? The text explicitly says it is 'ghayr lazim' (non-binding). Understand the implication: the imam can revoke it for maslaha.
3
Distinguish the two types
The passage divides aman into absolute (muṭlaq) and time-bound (muwaqqat). How is each terminated? Absolute: revocation by imam or enemy reneging. Time-bound: automatic expiry.
4
Apply to a scenario
Given a change in maslaha or expiry of time, trace the steps the imam must follow: inform, return to safety, then fight.
The principle of avoiding treachery (ghadr) governs the process.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما صفته فهو عقد غير لازم حتى لو رأى الإمام المصلحة في نقضه نقضه؛ كذا في البدائع قوله : (وننبذ لو شرا) أي نقض الإمام الأمان لو كان بقاؤه شراً لأن جوازه كان للمصلحة . أنه يتضمن ترك القتال مع المفروض فإذا صارت المصلحة في نقضه نقض وعبارة المصنف شاملة لما إذا اعطى الإمام الأمان لمصلحة ثم رأى المصلحة في نقضه ولما إذا أمنهم مسلم بغير إذن الإمام ولا مصلحة فيه، فاقتصار الشارح على الثاني مما لا ينبغي. وإذا فعله الواحد ولا مصلحة فيه أدبه الإمام لانفراده برأيه بخلاف ما إذا كان فيه مصلحة لأنه ربما تفوت بالتأخير فيعذر. وفي البدائع : إن الأمان على وجهين : مطلق وموقت ; فالأول ينتقض بأمرين : إما ينقض الإمام وينبغي أن يخبرهم به ثم يقاتلهم خوفاً من الغدر، وإما بمجيء أهل الحصن إلى الإمام بالأمان ثم امتناعهم عن الإسلام وقبول الجزية فإنه ينتقض لكن يردهم إلى مأمنهم ثم يقاتلهم احترازاً عن التغرير، فإن امتنعوا أن يلحقوا بمأمنهم أجلهم على ما يرى فإن لم يرجعوا حتى مضى الأجل صاروا ذمة. والثاني ينتهي بمضي الوقت من غير توقف على النقض، ولهم أن يقاتلوهم إلا إذا دخل واحد منهم الإسلام فمضى الوقت وهو فيه فهو آمن حتى يرجع إلى مأمنه .
As for its attribute, it is a non-binding contract, such that if the imam sees maslaha in revoking it, he revokes it; thus in al-Bada'i'. He said: (And we rescind if it becomes evil) meaning the imam revokes the aman if its continuation becomes evil, because its permissibility was due to maslaha. For it entails abandoning fighting against the appointed enemy, so when maslaha lies in revoking it, he revokes it. And the author's expression includes both when the imam granted aman for a maslaha and then sees maslaha in revoking it, and when a Muslim gave aman without the imam's permission and there is no maslaha in it, so the commentator's restriction to the second is not appropriate. And if one individual does it without maslaha, the imam disciplines him for acting on his own opinion, unlike if there is maslaha, because perhaps it may be lost by delay, so he is excused. And in al-Bada'i': Verily aman is of two types: absolute and time-bound. The first is nullified by two things: either the imam revokes it, and he should inform them of it and then fight them, fearing treachery; or when the people of the fortress come to the imam with aman and then refuse Islam and payment of jizya, it is nullified, but he returns them to their safe place and then fights them, as a precaution against deception. If they refuse to go to their safe place, he gives them a deadline as he sees fit; if they do not return until the deadline passes, they become dhimmis. The second type ends with the passing of time without needing revocation, and they may fight them, except if one of them entered Islam and the time passed while he was in it, then he is safe until he returns to his safe place.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling on the nature of aman (safe conduct). It first establishes that aman is a non-binding contract (ghayr lazim) in the Hanafi school, meaning the imam can revoke it if the public interest (maslaha) demands. The justification is that aman involves postponing fighting against the enemy, and if the maslaha changes, revocation is necessary. The text criticizes a commentator who restricted the discussion to the case where aman is given without imam's permission and without maslaha, whereas the author's wording also covers the case where the imam himself granted it for a maslaha and later sees maslaha in revoking it. An individual Muslim who grants aman without maslaha is disciplined by the imam, but if there is maslaha, he is excused. The passage then presents the division of aman from al-Bada'i' into two types: (1) absolute (mutlaq), which can be revoked by the imam (after informing the enemy to avoid treachery) or become void if the enemy reneges on Islam or jizya; and (2) time-bound (muwaqqat), which ends automatically when the time expires without need for revocation. If a person embraces Islam during the term, he remains safe until he returns to his homeland.

Key Terms
أمان (amān): Safe conduct granted to enemies; a non-binding contract revocable for maslaha.
مطلق (muṭlaq): Absolute aman without time limit; revocable by imam or voided by enemy's reneging.
موقت (muwaqqat): Time-bound aman that ends automatically with the expiry of the term.
مصلحة (maṣlaḥa): Public interest or benefit that justifies a ruling or its change.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The aman becomes void immediately because the enemy reneged.
B) The aman remains until the month ends, then the imam may fight after returning them to safety.
C) The imam must fight immediately without waiting.
D) The imam must extend the aman indefinitely.

Key Takeaway
Aman is a revocable, non-binding contract in the Hanafi school, classified as absolute or time-bound, with specific termination rules based on maslaha.

Invalidity of Aman from Dhimmi, Prisoner, Trader, Slave, and Restricted
Lists invalid aman with reasoning and intra-Hanafi differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state whose aman is invalid according to the Hanafi school, explain the reasoning based on the condition of fear, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the dhimmi's and slave's aman.

Core Idea
Aman is only valid if the giver inspires fear; those who do not are disqualified.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq lists five types of people whose grant of aman (safe conduct) to enemy combatants is invalid: the dhimmi (non-Muslim subject), the prisoner of war, the trader, the slave, and one restricted from fighting. The common reason is that these individuals do not inspire fear in the enemy, a key condition for aman. The passage also presents important intra-Hanafi differences, particularly regarding the dhimmi when authorized by the imam, and the slave if permitted to fight. The latter part discusses linguistic nuances in the wording used when seeking aman for oneself and others.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five categories and their common defect
List the five people: dhimmi, prisoner, trader, slave, and one restricted from fighting. Note the stated reason: they do not inspire fear – the dhimmi is suspect and has no authority, the prisoner and trader are under enemy control, the restricted slave is not feared.
The condition for aman is that the giver must be capable of inspiring fear (khawf).
2
Understand the exception for the dhimmi when authorized
Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that if the commander orders the dhimmi to give aman, it is valid. This is an intra-Hanafi correction to Abu Hanifa's absolute invalidity. Note the condition: permission from the imam.
The text says 'Wa sahhaha Muhammad amānahu' – Muhammad corrected (validated) his aman.
3
Analyze the ruling for the slave
A slave restricted from fighting cannot give valid aman. But if permitted by his master to fight, his aman is valid because he is then a potential combatant who can be feared.
This also reflects a difference: Muhammad's view considers permission key.
4
Apply the linguistic examples to aman wording
The latter part discusses how different wordings (e.g., 'give us aman', 'give me aman for ten', 'in ten of my brothers') affect whether the aman covers the speaker alone or includes others. The analysis turns on pronouns and particles. This is a practical application of the general principle.
The goal is to determine exactly who is covered by the aman based on the wording.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وبطل أمان ذمي وأسير وتاجر وعبد ومحجور عن القتال) لأن الذمي لا ولاية له على المسلمين وهو متهم والاسير والتاجر مقهوران تحت أيديهم فلا يخافونهم والأمان يختص بمحل الخوف والعبد المحجور عن القتال لا يخافونه فلا يلاقي الأمان محله بخلاف المأذون في القتال لأن الخوف منه متحقق، وصحح محمد أمانه قيد بكون الأمان من الذمي لأن الأمير لو أمر الذمي بأن يؤمنهم فأمنهم فهو جائز والمسألة على وجهين : إما أن يقول له قل لهم إن الذرية دون اسم الأهل لكن المثال الذي ذكره بقوله وإن قالوا أمنونا دخل فيه الطالبون لذكرهم أنفسهم بلفظ الكناية بخلاف مثال الأهل السابق فإنه ليس فيه ذلك وقد قال السرخسي أيضاً قبل ذلك : وإذا قالوا أمنونا على أهلينا ومتاعنا على أن نفتح لكم ففعلوا وفتحوا لهم فالقوم آمنون وإن لم يذكروا أنفسهم لأن النون والألف في أمنونا كناية وكلمة (على) للشرط فتقدير كلامهم نحن أمنون مع أهلينا وأموالنا . إن فتحنا لكم . ثم قال بعد خمسة أبواب : لو قال رئيس الحصن أمنوني على عشرة من أهل الحصن فقالوا لك ذلك فهو آمن وعشرة معه لأنه استأمن لنفسه نصاً بقوله أمنوني وقوله على عشرة للشرط وقد شرط أمان عشرة منكرة مع أمان نفسه فعرفنا أن العشرة سواه والخيار في تعيينهم له. ولو قال أمنوا لي عشرة فله عشرة يختارهم، فإن اختار عشرة هو أحدهم جاز أو عشرة سواه فهو فيء. وإن قال أمنوني وعشرة فالأمان له ولعشرة سواه، والخيار في تعيينهم للإمام ، وكذا أمنوني مع عشرة» وإن قال أمنوني في عشرة من أهل بيتي أو قال من بني أبي كان هو وتسعة سواه لأنه من جملة أهل بيته وبني أبيه والبيان للإمام. ولو قال في عشرة من إخواني فهو آمن وعشرة سواه لأن الإنسان لا يكون من إخوانه فوجب أن يجعل حرف في بمعنى مع لتعذر العمل بحقيقة الظرف، وكذا لو قال في عشرة من ولدي لأنه لا يكون من ولد نفسه قوله : (كانت خدمته أمانا له الظاهر أن المراد أنه يكون أماناً له في حق العبد نفسه لا في حق باقي المسلمين كما ظنه بعض الفضلاء فاستشكله تأمل .
He said: (And the aman of a dhimmi, a prisoner, a trader, a slave, and one restricted from fighting becomes void) because the dhimmi has no authority over Muslims and is suspect; the prisoner and trader are subjugated under their hands, so they are not feared; and aman is specific to a place of fear. The slave restricted from fighting is not feared, so aman does not meet its place, unlike one permitted to fight because fear from him is realized. Muhammad corrected his aman (i.e., the dhimmi's) with the condition that if the commander ordered the dhimmi to give them aman and he did, it is permissible. The issue has two aspects: either he says to him 'tell them that'... the offspring without the name of the family, but the example he mentioned: 'if they said 'give us aman'' includes the requesters because they mentioned themselves by a pronoun, unlike the previous example of the family because it does not have that. And al-Sarakhsi said before that: if they said 'give us aman for our families and goods on condition that we open for you' and they did and opened for them, then the people are safe even if they did not mention themselves because the letters 'nūn' and 'alif' in 'āmennā' are a pronoun and the word 'alā' is for condition, so their speech is 'we are safe with our families and our goods if we open for you'. Then he said after five chapters: if the chief of the fortress said 'give me aman for ten of the people of the fortress' and they said 'that is for you', he is safe and ten with him because he sought aman for himself explicitly by saying 'give me aman' and his saying 'for ten' is a condition, and he conditioned aman for ten unspecified with his own aman, so we know that the ten are other than him, and the choice of their specification is for him. And if he said 'give aman for me for ten', he has ten he chooses; if he chooses ten including himself, it is permissible; if ten other than him, then they are fay'. And if he said 'give me aman and ten', then aman is for him and ten other than him, and the choice of their specification is for the imam. Similarly, 'give me aman with ten'. And if he said 'give me aman in ten of my household' or said 'of my paternal uncles', he is safe and nine other than him because he is part of his household and paternal uncles, and the specification is for the imam. And if he said 'in ten of my brothers', he is safe and ten other than him because a person is not from his brothers, so the particle 'fī' must be taken in the sense of 'with' because it is impossible to act on the literal meaning of the adverb. Similarly if he said 'in ten of my children' because he is not from his own child. His saying: (his service is aman for him) the apparent meaning is that it is aman for him with respect to the slave himself, not with respect to the rest of the Muslims, as some virtuous thought and found it problematic. Contemplate.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is a ruling about individuals whose aman (safe conduct) is invalid according to the Hanafi school, along with reasoning and intra-Hanafi differences. The text lists: dhimmi (non-Muslim subject of Islamic state), prisoner of war (asir), trader (tajir), slave (abd), and one restricted from fighting (mahjur an al-qital). The reason: aman requires that the giver inspire fear in the enemy, but these individuals cannot: the dhimmi has no authority over Muslims and is suspected; the prisoner and trader are under the enemy's control; the slave not permitted to fight is not feared. However, Muhammad al-Shaybani corrects this for the dhimmi: if the commander (amir) orders the dhimmi to give aman, it is valid. The text then discusses various examples of the wording used when seeking aman for oneself and others, analyzing the particles and pronouns to determine whom the aman covers. For instance, 'give us aman' (aaminūna) implies the speakers themselves. 'Give me aman for ten' gives the requester choice to include himself or not. 'Give me aman in ten of my brothers' is interpreted as 'with ten' because one is not his own brother. Finally, it addresses the question of a Muslim slave serving a non-Muslim master in dar al-harb: his service serves as aman for himself (the slave) but not for other Muslims. The text ends with a note that some scholars found this problematic.

Key Terms
ذمي (dhimmī): A non-Muslim subject living permanently in the Islamic state under a contract of protection (dhimma).
أسير (asīr): Captive of war held by the enemy; his aman is invalid because he is under duress.
عبد محجور عن القتال (ʿabd maḥjūr ʿan al-qitāl): A slave who is not permitted by his master to participate in fighting.
أمان (amān): Safe conduct; its validity depends on the giver's ability to inspire fear.
مقهور (maqhoor): Subjugated, under forceful control. Used to describe the prisoner and trader: they are under the enemy's hands.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the aman of a prisoner of war invalid?
A) Because he is not a Muslim.
B) Because he is under the enemy's control and cannot be feared.
C) Because he has no family to protect.
D) Because he is likely to be killed anyway.

Key Takeaway
The aman of those who do not inspire fear is invalid; only the commander can authorize a dhimmi's aman, and a slave's aman is valid only if permitted to fight.

Ghanima: Definition and Ruling on Khums
Defines ghanima and its ruling on khums.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ghanima and state its ruling regarding khums and exclusive distribution to warriors.

Core Idea
Ghanima requires khums; the rest belongs to warriors.

Property acquired from the enemy during active warfare is governed by specific rules. The Hanafi school distinguishes between ghanima (booty taken by force) and fay' (acquired after war ends). This lesson focuses on ghanima and its mandatory khums (one-fifth). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying the law of war and public finance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Locate the definition of ghanima in the source: property obtained from the people of shirk by force while warfare is ongoing.
Key condition: active war and forceful acquisition.
2
Extract the ruling on khums
Notice that the text says 'one-fifth is taken' (tukhammas). This establishes the obligation of khums on ghanima.
The khums is wajib, not fard, as it is based on zanni evidence.
3
Understand distribution after khums
After removing the khums, the remaining four-fifths are exclusively for the warriors who fought.
This is a right of the fighters, not a general public fund.
4
Contrast with fay' (optional)
Note that if the property had been acquired after war ceased, it would be fay' and not khumsed. This highlights the conditional nature of ghanima.
Fay' is covered in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب السير باب الغنائم وقسمتها. ما الله غنم - بكسر - غنماً بالضم وبالفتح وبالتحريك، وغنيمة وغنماناً بالضم الفوز بالشيء بلا مشقة اهـ. وفي المغرب: الغنيمة ما نيل من أهل الشرك، عن أبي عبيدة عنوة والحرب قائمة. وحكمها أن تخمس وسائرها بعد الخمس للغانمين خاصة والفيء ما نيل منهم بعدما تضع الحرب أوزارها وتصير الدار دار إسلام، وحكمه أن يكون لكافة المسلمين ولا يخمس اهـ.
Book of Siyar, Chapter of Booty and its Division. 'Ghana' (with a kasra on the first letter, ghanam with dammah, fatha, and with tashkeel, ghanimat and ghanaman with dammah) means obtaining something without hardship. End quote. In al-Mughrib: Ghanima is what is obtained from the people of shirk, according to Abu Ubayda, by force while warfare is ongoing. Its ruling is that one-fifth is taken and the rest after one-fifth is exclusively for the warriors. Fay' is what is obtained from them after warfare has ceased and the land becomes abode of Islam. Its ruling is that it belongs to all Muslims and no one-fifth is taken from it.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling statement. It distinguishes between ghanima (booty taken by force during active war) and fay' (property acquired after war ends, e.g., by treaty). The Hanafi ruling: ghanima requires khums (one-fifth to the state) and the rest is distributed among the fighters. Fay' is not khumsed and belongs to the entire Muslim community for public welfare. This distinction is foundational for the law of war and public finance.

Key Terms
الغنيمة (al-ghanima): Property taken from the enemy by force during active warfare.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on ghanima regarding khums?
A) It is not khumsed at all.
B) One-fifth (khums) is taken, and the rest is for the warriors.
C) Half is taken for the state.
D) It is entirely for the imam.

Key Takeaway
Ghanima must be khumsed; the remaining four-fifths are exclusively for the warriors who fought.

Fay': Definition and Ruling on Absence of Khums
Defines fay' and its ruling that it is not khumsed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define fay' and state its ruling that it belongs to all Muslims without khums.

Core Idea
Fay' is not khumsed; it is for the entire Muslim community.

Property acquired from non-Muslims after hostilities have ceased goes by a different ruling. Unlike ghanima, fay' is not subject to khums and belongs to the entire Muslim polity for public welfare. This lesson explains the definition and Hanafi ruling on fay', highlighting the key difference from ghanima.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition
Find the definition of fay' in the source: what is obtained from non-Muslims after warfare has ceased and the land becomes dar al-Islam.
Key condition: cessation of war, often through treaty or surrender.
2
Extract the ruling on khums
Note the explicit statement: 'no one-fifth is taken from it' (la yukhamma). This is the opposite of ghanima.
Fay' is not khumsed.
3
Understand the beneficiary
The text says it 'belongs to all Muslims' (kafat al-muslimin). This means it is a public fund, not exclusively for warriors.
The imam administers it for the general welfare.
4
Contrast with ghanima
Compare with ghanima: ghanima requires active war; fay' requires war to have ended. This leads to different rulings on khums and distribution.
This distinction is crucial for proper classification.

Source Text

In al-Mughrib: Ghanima is what is obtained from the people of shirk, according to Abu Ubayda, by force while warfare is ongoing. Its ruling is that one-fifth is taken and the rest after one-fifth is exclusively for the warriors. Fay' is what is obtained from them after warfare has ceased and the land becomes abode of Islam. The Hanafi ruling: ghanima requires khums (one-fifth to the state) and the rest is distributed among the fighters. Fay' is not khumsed and belongs to the entire Muslim community for public welfare. Imam's Option in Conquered Lands: Divide or Kharaj
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on lands conquered by force and explain the imam's discretion with evidence from the Prophet and Umar.

Core Idea
The imam may choose to divide conquered lands or impose kharaj; both options have prophetic and caliphal precedent.

This lesson examines a key ruling in Hanafi fiqh regarding lands acquired through military conquest. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that the imam has the discretion to either distribute the land among the warriors or leave it in the hands of the original owners while levying kharaj. We will explore the proofs, the debate with the Shafi'i school, and practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify what is being ruled: the imam's option (mubah) to either divide the land or leave it with kharaj and jizya.
2
Locate the dalil naqli
Find the proofs: the Prophet's division at Khaybar and Umar's decision at Sawad with sahabi consensus.
Both are acts (fi'l) of the Prophet and a sahabi with ijma sukti.
3
Recognize the ikhtilaf
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i holds that distribution is mandatory, as land is analogous to movables.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi rebuttal: kharaj compensates the warriors; long-term benefit for the community; analogy with captives where imam has options.
The text also discusses linguistic nuance of 'anwa.
5
Apply the ruling
The imam's choice depends on maslaha: division preferred when warriors are in need, otherwise leaving with kharaj is better for later generations.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ما فتح الإمام عنوة قسم بيننا أو أقر أهلها ووضع الجزية والخراج) أي الجزية على رؤوسهم والخراج على أراضيهم والعنوة القهر كما في القاموس. وبه اندفع في شروح الهداية فالقسمة اتباع لفعله عليه السلام بخيبر وعدمها اتباع لفعل عمر رضي عنه بسواد العراق بموافقة من الصحابة ولم يجد من خالفه وفي كل من ذلك قدوة فيتخير . وقيل : الأول هو الأولى عند حاجة الغانمين والثاني عند عدم الحاجة ليكون عدة في الزمان الثاني، ولا يخفى أن القسمة بعد إخراج الخمس قيد بالأراضي لأن في المنقول المجرد لا يجوز المن بالرد عليهم لأنه لم يرد به الشرع فيه وفي العقار خلاف الشافعي لأن في المن إبطال حق الغانمين أو ملكهم فلا يجوز من غير بدل يعادله، والخراج غير معادل لقلته بخلاف الرقاب لأن للإمام أن يبطل حقهم رأساً إما بالعوض القليل وإما بالقتل والحجة عليه ما روينا، ولأن فيه نظراً لهم لأنهم كالأكرة العاملة للمسلمين العالمة أنه يخطئ به الذين يأتون من بعد والخراج وإن قل حالاً فقد جل مآلاً والمؤن مرتفعة مع وهو المن عليهم برقابهم وأراضيهم فقط وقسمة الباقي لدوامه، وإن من عليهم بالرقاب والأراضي يدفع إليهم من المنقولات قدر ما يتهيأ لهم العمل ليخرج عن حد الكراهة قوله : بوجوه الزراعة كان معنى له الشارحون على أن هذا ليس تفسيراً له لغة لأنها من عنى يعنو عنوا ذل وخضع وهو لازم و«قهراً» متعد. قال في الفتح : وإنما المعنى فتح بلدة حال كون أهلها ذوي عنوة وذلك يستلزم قهر المسلمين لهم وفيه وضع المصدر موضع الحال وهو غير المطرد إلا في ألفاظ اشتهرت، وإطلاق اللازم وإرادة الملزوم في غير التعاريف بل ذلك في الإخبارات والوجه أنه مجاز فإن عنوة اشتهر في نفس القهر عند الفقهاء فجاز استعماله فيه تعريفاً .اهـ. وما قاله في البحر لا يصلح دافعاً إلا إذا حقيقياً لا مجازياً وليس في القاموس ما يعينه، وهذا لأن صاحب القاموس لا يميز بين الحقيقي والمجازي كما قال بعضهم بل يذكر المعاني جملة .اهـ. وكأنه أراد بالبعض ابن حجر المكي وقد قدمنا عبارته في أول فصل التعزير قلت لكن نقل في باب العشر والخراج عن الفارابي أنه من الأضداد يطلق على الطاعة والقهر ومثله ما في المصباح حيث قال : عنا يعنو عنوة إذا أخذ الشيء قهراً وكذا إذا أخذه صلحاً فهو من الأضداد وفتحت مكة عنوة أي قهراً .اهـ. قوله: (وهو المن عليهم برقابهم وأراضيهم فقط وقسمة الباقي هكذا وجدت هذه الجملة في بعض النسخ عقب قوله «فقد جل مآلا» وفي بعضها عقب قوله ليخرج عن حد الكراهة وهي الصواب.
His saying: 'What the Imam conquers by force, he divides among us or he leaves its people and imposes jizya and kharaj' means jizya on their heads and kharaj on their lands. 'Anwa means overpowering as in al-Qamus. By this, the objection in the commentaries of Hidayah is refuted. So division follows the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) at Khaybar, and not dividing follows the practice of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) in the Sawad of Iraq with the agreement of the Companions and no one opposed him, so in each there is an example to follow, thus the Imam may choose. And it is said that the first is preferable when the warriors are in need, and the second when there is no need so that it becomes a provision for the later time. And it is not hidden that division after taking out the khums is restricted to lands because in movable property it is not permissible to show favor by returning it to them because the Shari'ah has not permitted that in movables. In real estate there is a difference with al-Shafi'i because showing favor would nullify the right of the warriors or their ownership, so it is not permissible without an equivalent compensation. Kharaj is not equivalent due to its smallness, unlike the captives because the Imam can nullify their right entirely either for a small compensation or by killing. The proof against him is what we narrated, and because there is consideration for them as they become sharecroppers working for the Muslims, knowing that it will benefit those who come later. And kharaj, though small immediately, becomes great in the end, and expenses are removed. And the favor is on them only regarding their persons and lands, and the remainder is divided for continuity. And if he shows favor on their persons and lands, he gives them from movable goods enough to enable them to work to avoid the degree of dislike. His saying: 'with methods of agriculture' - the commentators said that this is not a linguistic interpretation because it comes from 'ana ya'nu 'anwan meaning humility and submission, which is intransitive, while 'qahran' is transitive. Al-Fath said: Rather the meaning is that a town is conquered while its people are of 'anwa, which entails the Muslims overpowering them. This uses the verbal noun in place of the state particle, which is not standard except in well-known expressions. Using the intransitive to imply the transitive is not used in definitions but rather in statements. The correct view is that it is metaphorical, because 'anwa has become well-known in the sense of overpowering among the jurists, so it is permissible to use it in defining. End quote. What was said in al-Bahr is not a valid refutation unless it is meant as literal not metaphorical, and al-Qamus does not specify this. This is because the author of al-Qamus does not distinguish between literal and metaphorical, as some said, but rather mentions meanings collectively. End quote. It seems that 'some' refers to Ibn Hajar al-Makki. I say: However, in the chapter of 'ushr and kharaj, it is quoted from al-Farabi that it is an antonym meaning both obedience and overpowering. Similarly in al-Misbah: 'Ana ya'nu 'anwatan means he took something by force, and also if he took it peacefully, so it is an antonym. Mecca was conquered 'anwatan meaning by force. End quote. His saying: 'And it is the favor on them regarding their persons and lands only, and division of the rest' - this sentence was found in some copies after his saying 'fa qad jalla ma'alan' and in others after his saying 'li yakhruja 'an haddi al-karahah' and the latter is correct.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute. It addresses the imam's discretion regarding lands conquered by force ('anwa). The Hanafi position: the imam may either divide the land among the warriors (like the Prophet at Khaybar) or leave the original owners in possession while imposing kharaj and jizya (like Caliph Umar in Sawad of Iraq). Both actions have precedent, so the imam may choose based on public interest. The text refutes the Shafi'i objection that leaving land without division is invalid because it nullifies the warriors' rights. The Hanafi response: kharaj serves as compensation, and the long-term benefit for Muslims outweighs immediate distribution. The passage also discusses the linguistic meaning of 'anwa, confirming it is used metaphorically for force.

Key Terms
عنوة ('anwa): By force, overpowering; used to describe conquest without treaty.
خراج (kharaj): Land tax imposed on conquered lands that remain in the hands of original owners.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on lands conquered by force ('anwa)?
A) They must be divided among the warriors immediately.
B) The imam may either divide them or leave them with kharaj.
C) They become fay' and are not distributed.
D) They must be returned to the original owners.

Key Takeaway
The imam has discretion to either divide conquered lands or impose kharaj, based on public interest and prophetic precedent.

Captives in Jihad: Imam's Options and Prohibitions
Explaining imam's options and prohibitions with an intra-Hanafi dispute on ransom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three options available to the imam for captives and explain why returning, ransoming, and gratuitous release are prohibited, including the intra-Hanafi dispute on ransom.

Core Idea
The imam may kill, enslave, or release as dhimmis; but returning, ransoming, or freeing without compensation is prohibited – the captive becomes booty belonging to the warriors.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq defines the legal options for dealing with captives of war. It affirms the imam’s authority to choose among three permissible actions, then clarifies three forbidden acts that would violate the warriors’ rights. We will examine the evidence and note an important internal difference among the Hanafi masters regarding ransom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three lawful options and their evidence
Find where the text states the imam may kill, enslave, or release as dhimmi. Note the proofs: prophetic precedent (killing) and benefit to Muslims (enslavement, dhimmi status).
The exception for mushrik Arabs and apostates is also mentioned.
2
Identify the three prohibited actions and their reasoning
The text prohibits returning to dar al-harb, ransoming (fida'), and gratuitous release (mann). Understand the rationale: strengthening the enemy and nullifying warriors' rights.
Ransom is prohibited even for rescuing a Muslim captive according to Abu Hanifa.
3
Understand the rights of the warriors over the captive as booty
The text explains that captivity establishes the right of the warriors (ghanimun) to the captive as booty. Therefore, any action that nullifies this right without compensation is invalid.
This is compared to other items of booty.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on ransoming captives
Abu Hanifa prohibits all ransoming, even to free Muslim captives, because it strengthens the enemy. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow it for the purpose of rescuing Muslims, citing the captives of Badr.
The text gives the Hanafi response: harm to the umma outweighs individual benefit.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position and its practical implications
The well-known (mashhur) position is prohibition. However, Imam Muhammad permits ransom when Muslims are in need. A modern fatwa may balance these views based on context.
The text mentions al-Siyar al-Kabir for the permissive view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو استرق أو تركهم أحراراً ذمة لنا يعني أن الإمام بالخيار إن شاء قتلهم لأنه عليه السلام قد قتل ولأن فيه حسم مادة الفساد، وإن شاء استرقهم لأن فيه دفع شرهم مع وفور المنفعة لأهل الإسلام وإن شاء تركهم أحراراً ذمة للمسلمين لما بينا إلا مشركي العرب والمرتدين فإنهم لا يسترقون ولا يكونون ذمة على ما نبين إن شاء الله تعالى، وليس له فيمن أسلم منهم إلا الاسترقاق لأن قتله أو وضع الجزية عليه بعد إسلامه لا يجوز قيد بكون الخيار للإمام لأنه ليس لواحد من الغزاة أن يقتل أسيراً بنفسه لأن الرأي فيه إلى الإمام فقد يرى مصلحة المسلمين في استرقاقه فليس له أن يفتات عليه وعلى هذا فلو قتل بلا ملجئ بأن خاف القاتل شر الأسير كان له أن يعزره إذا وقع على خلاف مقصوده ولكن لا يضمن بقتله شيئاً؛ كذا في فتح القدير. وفي القاموس الأسير الأخيذ والمقيد والمسجون والجمع أسرى وأسارى وأسرى قوله : (وحرم ردهم إلى دار الحرب والفداء والمن) لأن في ردهم تقويتهم على المسلمين الفداء بهم معونة الكفرة لأنه يعود حرباً علينا ودفع شر حرابه خير من استخلاص الأسير المسلم لأنه إذا بقي في أيديهم كان ابتلاء في حقه غير مضاف إلينا، والإعانة بدفع أسيرهم إليهم مضاف إلينا فلا يجوز عند الإمام أبي حنيفة، وجوزا أن يفادى أسرى المسلمين تخليصاً للمسلم وجوابه ما مر . أطلق في منع الفداء فشمل الشيخ الكبير الذي لا يرجى له نسل. وعن محمد جوازه كما في الولوالجية، وشمل إطلاق الحربي وأخذ المسلم الأسير عوضاً عنه واستنقاذه منا بمال نأخذه منه . قال في المغرب : فداه من الأسر فداء وفدى استنقذه منه بمال، والفدية اسم ذلك المال، والمفاداة بين اثنين يقال فاداه إذا أطلقه وأخذ فديته. وعن المبرد: المفاداة أن تدفع رجلاً وتأخذ رجلاً والفداء أن تشتريه وقيل هما بمعنى .اهـ. وفي الثاني خلاف ففي المشهور من المذهب لا يجوز. وفي السير الكبير : لا بأس به إذا كان بالمسلمين حاجة استدلالاً بأسرى بدر، ولو كان أسلم الأسير في أيدينا لا يفادى بمسلم أسير في أيديهم لأنه لا يفيد إلا إذا طابت نفسه به وهو مأمون على إسلامه، وأما المن فقال في القاموس : من عليه مناً أنعم واصطنع عنده صنيعة اهـ. واختلفت العبارات في المراد به هنا ففي فتح القدير : هو أن يطلقهم إلى دار الحرب بغير شيء. وفي غاية البيان والنهاية : هو الإنعام عليهم بأن يتركهم مجاناً بدون إجراء الأحكام عليهم من القتل والاسترقاق أو تركهم ذمة للمسلمين .اهـ. ولا يصح الأول في كلام المختصر لأنه هو عين قوله وحرم ردهم إلى دار الحرب وإنما حرم لأن بالأسر ثبت حق الغانمين فلا يجوز إبطال ذلك بغير عوض كسائر الأموال المغنومة. وقيد بفداء الكفار لأنه يجوز فداء أسرى المسلمين به الذين في دار الحرب بالدراهم والدنانير وما ليس فيه قوة للحرب كالثياب وغيرها قوله : (وفي الثاني (خلاف أي اشتراؤه بمال وسماه ثانياً نظراً إلى ما في عبارة المبرد. قوله :
Or he enslaves them or leaves them free as dhimmis for us. Meaning the Imam has the choice: if he wishes, he may kill them because the Prophet (peace be upon him) killed, and because it cuts off the source of corruption; if he wishes, he may enslave them because it repels their evil and brings abundant benefit to the Muslims; if he wishes, he may leave them free as dhimmis for the Muslims, as we have explained, except the mushrikin of the Arabs and apostates, for they are not enslaved nor do they become dhimmis, as we will explain if Allah wills. And he has no option regarding those who become Muslim among them except enslavement, because killing him or imposing jizya on him after his Islam is not permissible. It is specified that the choice belongs to the Imam because it is not for any individual fighter to kill a captive by himself, because the decision rests with the Imam. The Imam may see the benefit of the Muslims in enslaving him, so the fighter may not act independently. On this basis, if he kills without compulsion, such as if the killer feared the captive's harm, he may be disciplined if it goes against his intention, but he is not liable for anything for his killing. This is in Fath al-Qadir. In al-Qamus: al-asir is the captured, bound, imprisoned, plural asra, asara, asra. His saying: 'And it is prohibited to return them to dar al-harb, and ransoming, and gratuitous release' because returning them strengthens them against the Muslims; ransoming them is assisting the disbelievers because it becomes a war against us, and repelling the harm of his warfare is better than rescuing the Muslim captive because if he remains in their hands, it is a trial for him that is not attributed to us, while assisting by sending their captive to them is attributed to us, so it is not permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allowed ransoming Muslim captives to rescue the Muslim, and the response is what has passed. The prohibition of ransom is general, including the old man from whom no offspring is expected. From Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, there is permission as in al-Walwalijiyyah. The general also includes the harbi and taking a Muslim captive in exchange for him, and rescuing him from us with money we take from him. Al-Mughrib: 'Fada' means rescued him from captivity by paying money. Al-fidya is the name of that money. Al-mufadatal between two: fadahu means released him and took his ransom. From al-Mubarrad: al-mufadatal is to give a man and take a man, while al-fida' is to buy him. It is said they are synonymous. End quote. There is a difference of opinion on the second (i.e., purchasing with money; he called it second with reference to al-Mubarrad's expression). According to the well-known position of the school, it is not permissible. In al-Siyar al-Kabir: there is no harm if the Muslims are in need, by analogy with the captives of Badr. If the captive becomes Muslim in our hands, he is not to be ransomed for a Muslim captive in their hands, because it is of no benefit unless he is willing, and he is trusted for his Islam. As for al-mann, al-Qamus says: 'Manna' means bestowed a favor. End quote. The expressions differ as to what is meant here. In Fath al-Qadir: it is to release them to dar al-harb without anything. In Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Nihaya: it is to show favor by leaving them for free without executing the rulings on them of killing, enslavement, or leaving them as dhimmis. End quote. The first is not correct in the words of the mukhtasar because it is exactly his saying 'it is prohibited to return them to dar al-harb'. It is prohibited because with captivity the right of the warriors is established, so it may not be nullified without compensation, like other items of booty. The prohibition is restricted to ransoming the disbelievers because it is permissible to ransom Muslim captives in dar al-harb with dirhams, dinars, and items that have no military strength, like clothes etc. His saying: 'And in the second there is difference' i.e., purchasing him with money, and he called it second with reference to al-Mubarrad's expression. His saying:
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute. It covers the imam's options for captives: kill, enslave, or release as dhimmis (except mushrik Arabs and apostates). Only the imam decides; individual fighters may not act independently. Then it lists three prohibitions: returning captives to dar al-harb, ransoming them (fida'), and gratuitous release (mann). The text presents an intra-Hanafi difference: Imam Abu Hanifa forbids ransoming captives even to free Muslim captives, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow it for the purpose of rescuing Muslims. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the well-known view is prohibition, but Imam Muhammad allows it if Muslims are in need, citing the captives of Badr. The prohibition of mann is defined as releasing without any compensation, which nullifies the warriors' right to the captive as booty.

Key Terms
الفداء (al-fida'): Ransom: giving a disbeliever captive in exchange for a Muslim captive or paying money for their release.
المن (al-mann): Gratuitous release: freeing a captive without any compensation.
الاسترقاق (al-istirqāq): Enslavement of a captive.
الأسير (al-asīr): Captive, prisoner of war.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is ransoming a disbeliever captive prohibited even to rescue a Muslim captive?
A) It strengthens the enemy, which is a greater harm.
B) The captive must first convert to Islam.
C) The warriors have no right to the captive.
D) It is only prohibited if money is paid.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the captive becomes the property of the warriors, so the imam may only kill, enslave, or release as dhimmi, but cannot return, ransom, or release gratuitously without violating rights.
